text:
This recipe is OUTSTANDING!  I make minor changes to it and it comes out delicious everytime.  I use one 15oz can of diced tomatoes (w/Basil,Oregano,Garlic flavoring) in place of the Roma tomatoes, I use Romano cheese in place of the Parmesan and I use a total of 1/4 cup of oil instead of the 1/2 cup.  I love it with the turkey sausage but have also made it with grilled chicken.   This is now my favorite recipe!!!!

We have a new favorite! If youre looking for a sauage/pasta dish that isn't all smothered in tomato sauce, then this is for you! The boullion and tomatoes make such a light refreshing sauce that really brings out the other flavors! For best results, I wouldn't advise subbing dried basil for fresh, (flavor goes down to 3-4 stars w/dried). Great presentation/colors, too. Perfect for company! Thanks!!!

text:
What a wonderful dish! I presented it in a cooking class at church and received rave reviews. This recipe makes 7 cups and freezes well for the next go 'round. My modifications: bulk turkey Italian sausage, canned diced tomatoes with basil & garlic, zucchini and summer squash, broccoli, cauliflower & carrot mix, can of mushroom pieces, 1/4 c olive oil, green & red bell peppers and an Italian cheese blend w/ Parmesan, Asiago, Mozzarella and Provolone. This dish was 'tha bomb'!!

text:
This recipe surprised me with how tasty it was. I was just looking for a way to use up the squash from my garden! I had to use canned tomatoes since my garden is only offering green maters right now. I also left out the green pepper since I don't like it. I used much less olive oil and instead used the juice from the canned tomatoes when I needed more liquid. I can't have cheese right now (and how I love fresh parmesan!), but I don't think the dish suffered at all without it. Don't worry, I got my fat grams by using full-on hot Italian PORK sausage. I highly recommend using fresh basil. Fabulous taste and easy to make with a nice zing - a keeper!

text:
Both my fiance and myself really enjoyed this recipe.  I made some minor changes but I'm sure the recipe would be just as good as written.  Since I was cooking for two, I decreased the amount of ingredients.  I used 2 hot italian sausages, casings removed.  Crumbled the sausage while browning it in a saucepan and then set aside.  I added a little more evoo to the pan with the sausage grease and added 4 cloves of garlic and 1 small chopped white onion, then added 1 chopped zucchini, 1 yellow squash, 2 large chopped tomatos, 1 red pepper, and a handful of chopped fresh basil.  I also added some basic spices, salt, pepper and red pepper flakes.  After a few minutes I added a cup of chicken broth and about 1/2 cup white wine and let simmer for about 10-15 minutes.  Added some parmesan at the end and mixed in 1/2 pound penne pasta.  Will make this again and again!

This is a GREAT recipe!  Okay, actually, I didn't try this one because I changed it so much, but I know from my results this would have been awesome too!  My grocer didn't have basil that looked good, so I used a jar of imported basil pesto instead.  I used canned diced tomatoes, drained since we have a salmonella issue with tomatoes right now.  I also used sweet Italian sausage instead of hot and cut out the red pepper flakes so my 6 yr old could eat it.  Next time, I will probably use less olive oil - but then I did use it while sauteing the veggies and added it all to the pasta with pesto (which already has quite a bit of olive oil).  This recipe is versatile and would work with various combinations of veggies and types of pasta.  Thanks for the idea!  (Hey, at least I didn't give it a low rating based on MY changes!  :)

text:
This is a keeper although I made some minor adjustments.  16 ounces of pasta ended up being waaay to much, it never would have fit in my largest skillet with all the other ingredients, so I only put half of it in the mixture and refrigerated the rest for another use.  This didn't take away from the recipe at all, I thought the vegetable/pasta ratio was perfect with only half the pasta.  I cooked the pasta a couple minutes less than the package instructed so it could continue cooking in the vegetable mixture and absorb some of the flavor.  I originally didn't want to use all the oil that was called for, but ended up adding it all anyway because I doubled the Parmesan cheese and I don't think it would have melted right without the extra fat in there.  Resist to the temptation to add extra salt until you've added everything in and let it cook a few minutes.  The salt from the bullion and the cheese was just the right amount.

This is very yummy!!  My husband LOVED it!  I almost followed the recipe.  

I added a can of tomato sauce along with the second addition of olive oil in order to make it a little more saucy.  

I also used four-color radiatore instead of farfalle because radiatore was the only whole grain colored pasta I could find.  We loved the texture the radiatore provided cause it got soft very quickly and mixed in with the vegetables really well.  

I also used mild turkey italian sausage and left out the red pepper because I have a 2-year old and I figured anyone who wanted pepper could add it to their own.

Thank you for this great recipe!

This recipe has fantastic flavors and is relatively easy to make.  After making this a few times, it is also very flexible around what types of veggies to use.  If the zucchini and squash are not available a multi colored pepper mix works well. text:
I used mild Italian sausage and Rainbow Rotini instead of the Farfalla pasta recommended in the recipe. I also used a whole Valdalia onion and six cloves of garlic. I used only three Roma plum tomatoes but replaced them with 1/2 sweet red bell pepper and 1/2 orange bell pepper. This made it super colorful. Also only used about 1/8 cup olive oil and that was plenty! This was so fresh and well seasoned it needed no extra salt or pepper and we served the shaved paramasean cheese on the side to sprinkle on top at the table. I think this adds to the color and don't recommend heating the cheese in the pasta as the last step of the published recipe instructs. It turned out brilliantly colorful with fantastic flavor! I made this dish that serves eight and fed four of us....it was nearly gone!! I will definitely repeat this!

Made tonight for hubby and myself. This is a keeper! I really appreciate the suggestions of others and incorporated some of them. text:
Deliciously light and satisfying! I used crumbled basil & chicken sausages (casings removed) and ripe, sweet grape tomatoes (instead of romas). Also used chicken buillion paste (as I don't have granuals) and substituted asparagus for the yellow squash as it wasn't available at my store. I deglazed the pan with a little no-salt chicken broth after sauting the sausages, onion and garlic (to get up all those yummy bits). Added the basil at the very end (otherwise it gets mushy) and mixed everything together for maybe 3 min over medium heat. Served it with the Parmesan cheese sprinkled on top - what a hit! Hubby absolutely loved it and I did too. Definitely company worthy!

I make hundreds of things from this website, but have never rated one....no matter how good, till now. Super easy, super fresh, one pan (unless you count boiling the pasta) and it can stay warm for multiple shifts of family coming and going with sports and after school. My husband and kids all had extra helpings, and asked for it again today! Perfect weekday dinner.

My husband and I both really liked this recipe. I would recommend having everything chopped before starting to cook then you can gauge the doneness of the vegetables better.  I made a few little changes. I added garden green bean and broccoli to the suggested veg. Also changed green pepper to red. It took me 2 hours to make this dish but it was well worth the wait!  I had to really cut my sausage down and turn the heat up to get it cooked and my zucchini didn't want to get soft.  Not an issue with the recipe, the medium temperature recommended just didn't work for my skillet.  I had to use medium high and use a cover once I put in the zucchini. My son-in-law who hates veggies even cleaned his plate!  Yummy noises abounded during dinner which is the ultimate sign of a good dish.

text:
I don't use chicken bullion cubes, since they're loaded with salt and MSG (which causes food addiction), so I switched it to a half cup of organic chicken broth. I also prefer extreme flavor, so had to add a 1/2 teaspoon chili powder, a  pinch of ceyenne pepper, a pinch of sea salt and a teaspoon of black pepper. Basically, if it doesn't burn even a tiny bit, I won't eat it. In addition, I didn't have fresh basil at home (the plant died) but did have fresh parsley and cilantro, so I added a half cup of that as well, and as a replacement for the fresh basil. As I always say, "The fresher, the better." It was amazingly deliscious, and enough for 4 with leftovers.

text:
This recipe is delish! I don't understand what makes it so good... but it really is. We love it. A couple comments - definitely don't use all that oil! I just use a drizzle to coat the pan when cooking the garlic/onions and then another bigger drizzle when the veggies are cooking. The second drizzle probably isn't even necessary; the veggies produce their own liquid as they cook down.  Fresh basil makes it amazing; I've subbed dried basil in a pinch and it's still fine... but better w/ fresh. I also crumble the sausage when cooking instead of slicing it.. but that's a personal preference. This makes a TON of food and the leftovers taste just as good.  Thanks for the yummy recipe!

text:
All I can say is...WOW. This recipe surpassed my expectations. Even while I was making it, I was skeptical and didn't think it would amount to much. I was wrong! The recipe was bursting with flavor! I followed the recipe except I used a 15oz can of italian seasoned diced tomatoes and I only used squash (which my daughter didn't like so much). I also used the powdered parmesan instead of grated and sprinkled it over the dish after I put it on the plate. Also, I recommend browning the sausage first, setting aside to cool, then cutting. It was impossible to cut the sausage while it was raw. One last word, I didn't use the whole box of pasta, doing so would've made the dish VERY dry. Half was enough.
